<start> THE WILL TO POWER IN SCIENCE . <end>
<start> a The Method of Investigation . <end>
<start> The distinguishing feature of our nineteenth : i century is not the triumph of science , but the j triumph of the scientific method over science . <end>
<start> the history of scientific methods was regarded by Auguste Comte almost as philosophy itself . <end>
<start> The great methodologies : Aristotle , Bacon , Descartes , Auguste Comte . <end>
<start> The most valuable knowledge is always discovered last : but the most valuable knowledge consists of methods . <end>
<start> All methods , all the hypotheses on which the science of our day depends , were treated with the profoundest contempt for centuries : on their account a man used to be banished from the society of respectable people he was held to be an enemy of God a reviled of the highest ideal , a madman . <end>
<start> We had the whole pathos of mankind against us , our notion of what truth ought to be , of what the service of truth ought to be , our objectivity , our method , our calm , cautious and distrustful manner were altogether despicable . <end>
<start> At bottom , that which has kept men back most , is an aesthetic taste : they believed in the picturesque effect of truth what they demanded of the scientist was , that he should make a strong appeal to their imagination . <end>
<start> From the above , it would almost seem as if the very reverse had been achieved , as if a sudden jump had been made : as a matter of fact , the schooling which the moral hyperbole afforded , gradually prepared the way for that milder form of pathos which at last became incarnate in the scientific man . <end>
<start> Conscientiousness in small things , the self control of the religious man , was a preparatory school for the scientific character , as was also , in a very pre eminent sense , the attitude of mind which makes a man take problems seriously irrespective of what personal advantage he may derive from them . <end>
<start> b The Starting point of Epistemology . <end>
<start> Profound disinclination to halt once and for all at any collective view of the world . <end>
<start> The charm of the opposite point of view : the refusal to relinquish the stimulus residing in the enigmatic . <end>
<start> The hypothesis that , at bottom , things proceed in such a moral fashion that human reason must be rights is a mere piece of good natured and simple minded truthfulness , the result of the belief in Divine truthfulness God regarded as the Creator of all things . <end>
<start> These concepts are our inheritance from a former existence in a Beyond . <end>
<start> The contradiction of the so called facts of consciousness . <end>
<start> Observation a thousand times more difficult , error is perhaps the absolute condition of observation . <end>
<start> The intellect cannon criticise itself , simply because it can be compared with no other kind of intellect , and also because its ability to know , A P would only reveal itself in the presence of actual reality that is to say , because , in order to criticise the intellect , we should have to be higher creatures with absolute knowledge . <end>
<start> This would presuppose the existence of something , a thingie itself , apart from all the perspective kinds of observation and sense spiritual perception . <end>
<start> But the psychological origin of the belief in things , forbids our speaking of things in themselves . <end>
<start> The idea that a sort of adequate relation exists between subject and object , that the object is something which when seen from inside would be a subject , is a well meant invention which , I believe , has seen its best days . <end>
<start> The measure of that which we are conscious of , is perforce entirely dependent upon the coarse utility of the function of consciousness : how could this little of consciousness warrant our asserting anything in regard to subject and object , which would bear any relation to reality ! <end>
<start> Criticism of modern philosophy : erroneous starting point , as if there were such things as facts of consciousness and no phenomenalism in introspection . <end>
<start> Consciousness to what extent is the idea which is thought of , the idea of will , or the idea of a feeling which is known by us alone , quite superficial ? <end>
<start> Our inner world is also appearance THE WILL TO POWER IN SCIENCE . <end>
<start> d I am convinced of the phenomenalism of the inner world also : everything that reaches our consciousness is utterly and completely adjusted , simplified , , interpreted , the actual process of inner perception , the relation of causes between thoughts , feelings , desires , between subject and object , is absolutely concealed from us , and I may be purely imaginary . <end>
<start> This inner world of appearance is treated with precisely the same forms and procedures as the outer world . <end>
<start> We never come across a single fact : pleasure and pain are more recently evolved intellectual phenomena . <end>
<start> Causality evades us to assume the existence of an immediate causal relation between thoughts , as Logic does , is the result of the coarsest and most clumsy observation . <end>
<start> There are all sorts of passions that may intervene between two thoughts : but the interaction is too rapid that is why we fail to recognise them , that is why we actually deny their existence . <end>
<start> Thinking , as the understand it , never takes place at all : it is an absolutely gratuitous fabrication , arrived at by selecting one element from the process and by eliminating all the rest an artificial adjustment for the purpose of the understanding . <end>
<start> The mind , something that thinks : at times , even , the mind absolute and pure this concept is an evolved and second result of false introspection , which believes in thinking : in the first place an act is imagined here which does not really occur at all , i . <end>
<start> e . <end>
<start> thinking and , secondly , a subject substratum is imagined in which every p cess of this thinking has its origin , and nothing else that is to say , both the action and the agent are fanciful . <end>
<start> Phenomenalism must not be sought in the wrong quarter : nothing is more phenomenal , to be more precise , nothing is so much deception , as this inner world , which we observe with the inner sense . <end>
<start> Our belief that the will is a cause was so great , that , according to our personal experiences in general , we projected a cause into all phenomena i . <end>
<start> e . <end>
<start> a certain motive is posited as the cause of all phenomena . <end>
<start> We believe that the thoughts which follow one upon the other in our minds are linked by some sort of causal relation : the logician , more especially , who actually speaks of a host of facts which have never once been seen in reality , has grown accustomed to the prejudice that thoughts are the cause of thoughts . <end>
<start> We believe and even our philosophers believe it still that pleasure and pain are the causes of reactions , that the very purpose of pleasure and pain is to occasion reactions . <end>
<start> For hundreds of years , pleasure and pain have been represented as the motives for every action . <end>
<start> Upon reflection , however , we are bound to concede that everything would have proceeded in exactly the same way , according to precisely the same sequence of cassette WILL TO POWER IN SCIENCE . <end>
<start> and effect , if the states pleasure and pain had been entirely absent and that we are simply deceived when we believe that they actually cause anything : they are the attendant phenomena , and they have quite a different purpose from that of provoking reactions they are in themselves effects involved in the process of reaction which takes place . <end>
<start> In short : Everything that becomes conscious is a final phenomenon , a conclusion and is the cause of nothing all succession of phenomena in consciousness is absolutely atomistic . <end>
<start> And we tried to understand the universe from the opposite point of view as if nothing were effective or real , save thinking , feeling , willing ! <end>
<start> The phenomenalism of the inner world ? <end>
<start> A chronological inversion takes place , so that the cause reaches consciousness as the effect . <end>
<start> We r know that pain is projected into a certain part of the body although it is not really situated there we have learnt that all sensations which were ingenuously supposed to be conditioned by the outer world are , as a matter of fact , conditioned by the inner world : that the real action of the ? <end>
<start> outer world never takes place in a way of which we can become conscious . <end>
<start> That fragment of the outer world of which we become conscious , is born after the effect produced by the outer world has been recorded , and is subsequently interpreted as the cause of that effect . <end>
<start> hIn the phenomenalism of the inner world , the chronological order of cause and effect is inverted . <end>
<start> The fundamental fact of inner experience is , that the cause is imagined after the effect has been recorded . <end>
<start> The same holds good of the sequence of thoughts : we seek for the reason of a thought , before it has reached our consciousness and then the reason reaches consciousness first , whereupon follows its effect . <end>
<start> All our dreams are the interpretation of our collective feelings with the view of discovering the possible causes of the latter and the process is such that a condition only becomes conscious , when the supposed causal link has reached consciousness . <end>
<start> The whole of inner experience is founded on v i this : that a cause is sought and imagined which I accounts for a certain irritation in our nerve centres , and that it is only the cause which is found in this way which reaches consciousness this cause may have absolutely nothing to do with the real cause it is a sort of groping assisted by former inner experiences , that is to say , by memory . <end>
<start> The memory , however , retains the habit of old interpretations , that is to say , of erroneous causality , I so that inner experience comprises in itself all the results of former erroneous fabrications of causes . <end>
<start> Our outside world , as we conceive it every instant , is indissolubly bound up with the When in our dream we hear a bell ringing , or a tapping at our door , we scarcely ever wake before having already accounted for the sound , in the terms of the dream world we were in . <end>

<start> Inner experience only enters consciousness when it has found a language which the individual can understand that is to say , a translation of a certain condition into conditions with which he is familiar understand means simply this : to be able to express something new in the terms of something old or familiar . <end>
<start> For instance , I feel unwell a judgment of this sort presupposes a very great and recent neutrality on the part of the observer : the simple man always says , This and that make me feel unwell , he begins to be clear concerning his indisposition only after he has discovered a reason for it . <end>
<start> This is what I call a lack of philological knowledge to be able to read a text , as such , without reading an interpretation into it , is the latest form of inner experience , it is perhaps a barely possible form . <end>
<start> There are no such things as mind , reason , thought , consciousness , soul , will , or truth : they all belong to fiction , and can serve no purpose . <end>

<start> Perspectivity . <end>
<start> It is our needs that interpret the world our instincts and their impulses for and against . <end>
<start> Every instinct is a sort of thirst for power each has its point of view , which it would fain impose upon all the other instincts as their norm . <end>
<start> I Where our ignorance really begins , at that point from which we can see no further , we set a word for instance , the word I , the word do , the word suffer these concepts may be the horizon lines of our knowledge , but they are not truths . <end>
<start> Owing to the phenomenon thought , the ego is taken for granted but up to the present everybody believed , like the people , that there was something unconditionally certain in the notion I think , and that by analogy with our understanding of all other causal reactions this I was the given cause of the thinking . <end>
<start> However customary and indispensable this fiction may have become now , this fact proves nothing against the imagine are nature of its origin it might be a life preserving belief and still be false . <end>
<start> Something is thought , therefore there is something that thinks : this is what Descartes argument amounts to . <end>
<start> But this is tantamount to considering our belief in the notion substance as an a prior truth : that there must be something that thinks when we think , is merely a formulation of a grammatical custom which sets an agent to every action . <end>
<start> In short , a metaphysics logical postulate is already put forward here and it is not merely an ascertainment of fact . <end>
<start> On Descartes lines nothing absolutely certain is attained , but only the fact of a very powerful faith . <end>
<start> If the proposition be reduced to Something is thought , therefore there are thoughts , the result is mere tautology and precisely the one factor which is in question , the reality of thought , is not touched upon , so that , in this form , the apparition character of thought cannon be denied . <end>
<start> What Descartes wanted to prove was , that thought not only had apparent reality , but absolute reality . <end>
<start> The concept substance is an outcome of the concept subject , and not conversely ! <end>
<start> If we surrender the concept soul , the subject , the very conditions for the concept substance are lacking . <end>
<start> Degrees of Being are obtained , but Being is lost . <end>
<start> Criticism of reality : what does a plus or minus of reality lead to , the gradation of Being in which we believe ? <end>
<start> The degree of our feeling of life and power the logic and relationship of past life presents us with the measure of Being , reality , non-appearance . <end>
<start> Subject : this is the term we apply to our belief in an entity underlying all the different moments of the most intense sensations of reality : we regard this belief as the effect of a cause , and we believe in our belief to such an extent that , on its account alone , we imagine truth , reality , substantially . <end>
<start> Subject is the fiction which would fain make us believe that several similar states were the effect of one substratum : but we it was who first created the similarity of these states the civilising and adjusting of them is the fact not their similarity on the contrary , this ought rather to be denied . <end>
<start> One would have to know what Being is , in order to be able to decide whether this or that , is real for instance , the facts of consciousness j it would also be necessary to know what certainty and knowledge are , and so forth . <end>
<start> But , as we do I not know these things , a criticism of the faculty of knowledge is nonsensical : how is it possible for an instrument to criticise itself , when it is itself that exercises the critical faculty . <end>
<start> It cannon even de I fine itself ! <end>

<start> to abandon it would mean to cease from being able to think . <end>
<start> But that a belief , however useful it may be for the preservation of a species , has nothing to do with the truth , may be seen from the fact that we must believe in time , space , and motion , without feeling ourselves compelled to regard them as absolute realities . <end>

<start> The foul blemish on Kant s criticism has at last become visible even to the coarsest eyes : Kant had no right to his distinction appearance and thing in itself in his own writings he had deprived himself of the right of differentiating any longer in this old and hackneyed manner , seeing that he had condemned the practice of drawing any conclusions concerning the cause of an appearance from the appearance itself , as allowable in accordance with his conception of the idea of causality and its purely validity : and this conception , on the other hand , already anticipates that differentiation , as if the thing itself were not only inferred but actually given . <end>

<start> The aberrations of philosophy are the outcome of the fact that , instead of recognising in logic and the categories of reason merely a means to the adjustment of the world for utilitarian ends that is to say , especially , a useful falsification , they were taken to be the criterion of truth particularly of reality . <end>
<start> The criterion of truth was , as a matter of fact , merely the biological utility of a systematic falsification of this sort , on principle : and , since a species of animals knows nothing more important than its own preservation , it was indeed allowable here to speak of truth . <end>

<start> The Mechanical Interpretation of the World . <end>
<start> Of all the interpretations of the world attempted heretofore , the mechanical one seems to day to stand most prominently in the front . <end>
<start> Apparently it has a clean conscience on its side for no science believes inwardly in progress and success unless it be with the help of mechanical procedures . <end>
<start> Every one knows these procedures : reason and purpose are allowed to remain out of consideration as far as possible it is shown that , provided a sufficient amount of time be allowed to elapse , everything can evolve out of everything else , and no one attempts to suppress his malicious satisfaction , when the apparent design in the fate of a plant or of of an egg , may be traced to stress and thrust in short , people are heartily glad to pay respect to this principle of profoundest stupidity , if I may be allowed to pass a playful remark concerning these serious matters . <end>
<start> Meanwhile , among the most select intellects to be found in this move ment , some presentiment of evil , some anxiety is noticeable , as if the theory had a rent in it , which sooner or later might be its last : I mean the sort of rent which denotes the end of all balloons inflated with such theories . <end>
<start> Stress and thrust themselves cannon be explained , one cannon get rid of the actio in distant . <end>
<start> The belief even in the ability to explain is now lost , and people peevishly admit that one can only describe , not explain that the dynamic interpretation of the world , with its denial of empty space and its little agglomerations of atoms , will soon get the better of physicists : although in this way dynamic is certainly granted an inner quality . <end>
<start> The triumphant concept energy with which our physicists created God and the world , needs yet to be completed : it must be given an inner will which I characterise as the Will to Power that is to say , as an insatiable desire to manifest power or the application and exercise of power as a creative instinct , etc . <end>
<start> Physicists cannon get rid of the actio in distant in their principles any more than they can a repelling force or an attracting one . <end>
<start> There is no help for it , all movements , all appearances , all laws must be understood as symptoms of an inner phenomenon , and the analogy of man must be used for this purpose . <end>
<start> It is possible to trace all the instincts of an animal to the will to power as also all the functions of organic life to this one source . <end>
<start> THE WILL TO POWER IN NATURE . <end>
<start> villas anybody ever been able to testify to a force ? <end>
<start> No , but to effects , translated into a completely strange language . <end>
<start> Regularity in sequence has so spoilt us , that we no longer wonder at the wonderful process . <end>
<start> A force of which we cannon form any idea , is an empty word , and ought to have no civic rights in the city of science : and the same applies to the purely mechanical powers of attracting and repelling by means of which we can form an image of the world no more ! <end>
<start> Squeezes and kicks are something incalculable recent , evolved and not primeval . <end>
<start> They presuppose something which holds together and can press and strike ! <end>
<start> But how could it hold together ? <end>
<start> There is nothing unalterable in chemistry : this is only appearance , a mere school prejudice . <end>
<start> We it was who introduced the unalterable , taking it from metaphysics as usual , Mr . <end>
<start> Chemist . <end>
<start> It is a mere superficial judgment to declare that the diamond , graphite , and carbon are identical . <end>
<start> Why ? <end>
<start> Simply because no loss of substance can be traced in the scales ! <end>
<start> Well then , at least they have something in common but the work of the molecules in the process of changing from one form to the other , an action we can neither see nor weigh , is just exactly what makes one material something different with specifically different qualities . <end>
<start> Against the physical atom . <end>
<start> In order to understand the world , we must be able , to reckon it up in order to be able to reckon it up , we must be aware of constant causes but since we find no such constant causes in reality , we invent them for ourselves and call them atoms . <end>
<start> This is the origin of the atomic theory . <end>
<start> The possibility of calculating the world , the possibility of expressing all phenomena by means of formulas is that really understanding ? <end>
<start> What would be understood of a piece of music , if all that were calculable in it and capable of being expressed in formulae , were reckoned up ? <end>
<start> Thus constant causes , things , substances , something unconditioned , were therefore invented what has been attained thereby ? <end>
<start> The mechanical concept of movement is already a translation of the original process into the language of symbols of the eye and the touch . <end>
<start> The concept atom , the distinction between the seat of a motive force and the force itself , is a language of symbols derived from our logical and psychical world . <end>
<start> means of expression : it is possible to understand to what extend they are but symptomatic . <end>
<start> To demand an adequate means of expression is nonsense : it lies at the heart of a language , of a medium of communication , to express relation only . <end>
<start> The concept truth is opposed to good sense . <end>
<start> The whole province of truth falseness only applies to the relations between beings , not to an absolute . <end>
<start> There is no such thing as a being in ? <end>
<start> itself relations in the first place constitute being , any more than there can be knowledge in itself . <end>
<start> The feeling of force cannon proceed from movement : feeling in general cannon proceed from movement Even in support of this , an apparent experience is the only evidence : in a substance brain feeling is generated through transmitted motion stimuli . <end>
<start> But generated ? <end>
<start> Would this show that the feeling did not yet exist there at all so that its appearance would have to be regarded as the creative act of the intermediary motion ? <end>
<start> The condition of this substance is only an hypothesis ! <end>
<start> not an experience ! <end>
<start> Feeling , therefore is the quality of the substance : there actually are substances that feel . <end>
<start> Do we learn from certain substances that they have no feeling ? <end>
<start> No , we merely cannon tell that they have any . <end>
<start> It is impossible to seek the origin of feeling in non sensitive substance . <end>
<start> Oh what nastiness ! <end>
<start> To attract and M to repel , in a purely mechanical sense , is pure fiction : a word . <end>
<start> We cannon imagine an attraction without a purpose . <end>
<start> Either the will to possess one s self of a thing , or the will to defend one s self from a thing or to repel it that we understand : that would be an interpretation which we could use . <end>
<start> In short , the psychological necessity of believing in causality lies in the impossibility of imagining a process without a purpose : but of course this says nothing concerning truth or untruth the justification of such a belief ! <end>
<start> The belief in causes collapses with the belief in term against Spinoza and his . <end>
<start> It is an illusion to suppose that something is known , when all we have is a mathematical formula of what has happened : it is only characterised , described no more ! <end>
<start> If I bring a regularly recurring phenomenon into a formula , I have facilitated and shortened my task of characterising the whole phenomenon , etc . <end>
<start> But I have not thereby ascertained a law , I have only replied to the question : How is it that something recurs here ? <end>
<start> It is a supposition that the formula corresponds to a complex of really unknown forces and the discharge of forces : it is pure mythology to suppose that forces here obey a law , so that , as the result of their obedience , we have the same phenomenon every time . <end>
<start> I take good care not speak of chemical laws : to do so savours of morality . <end>
<start> It is much more a question of establishing certain relations of power : the stronger becomes master of the weaker , in so far as the latter cannon maintain its degree of independence , here there is no pity , no quarter , and , still less , any observance of law . <end>
<start> The unalterable sequence of certain phenomena does not prove any law , but a relation of power between two or more forces . <end>
<start> To say , But it is precisely this relation that remains the same ! <end>
<start> is no better than saying , One and the same force cannon be another force . <end>
<start> It is not a matter of sequence , but a matter of interdependence , a process in which the procession of moments do not determine each other after the manner of cause and effect . <end>
<start> Theseparation of the action from the agent of the phenomenon from the worker of that phenomenon of the process from one that is not process , but lasting , substance , thing , body , soul , etc . <end>
<start> the attempt to understand a life as a sort of shifting of things and a changing of places of a sort of being or stable entity : this ancient mythology established the belief in cause and effect , once it had found a lasting form in the functions of speech and grammar . <end>
<start> The regularity of a sequence is only a metaphorical expression , not a fact , just as if . <end>
<start> rule were followed here ! <end>
<start> And the same holds good of conformity to law . <end>
<start> We find a formula in order to express an ever recurring kind of succession of phenomena : but that does not show that we have discovered a law much less a force which is the cause of a recurrence of effects . <end>
<start> The fact that something always happens thus or thus , is interpreted here as if a creature always acted thus or thus as the result of obedience to a law or to a lawgiver : whereas apart from the law it would be free to act differently . <end>
<start> But precisely that inability to act otherwise might originate in the creature itself , it might be that it did not act thus or thus in response to a law , but simply because it was so constituted . <end>
<start> It would mean simply : that something cannon also be something else that it cannon be first this , and then something quite different that it is neither free nor the reverse , but merely thus or thus . <end>
<start> The fault lies in thinking a subject into things . <end>
<start> To speak of two consecutive states , the first as cause , and the second as effect , is false . <end>
<start> The first state cannon bring about anything , the second has nothing effected in it . <end>
<start> It is a question of a struggle between two elements unequal in power : a new adjustment is arrived at , according to the measure of power each possesses . <end>
<start> The second state is something fundamentally different from the first it is not its effect : the essential thing is , that the factors which engage in the struggle leave it with different quanta of power . <end>
<start> A criticism of Materialism . <end>
<start> Let us dismiss the two popular concepts , Necessity and Law , from this idea : the first introduces a false constraint , the second a false liberty into the world . <end>
<start> Things do not act regularly , they follow no rule : y there are no things that is our fiction neither do they act in accordance with any necessity . <end>
<start> There is no obedience here : for , the fact that something is as it is , strong or weak , is not the result of obedience or of a rule or of a constraint . <end>
<start> The degree of resistance and the degree of superior power this is the question around which all phenomena turn : if we , for our own purposes and calculations , know how to express this in formulae and laws , all the better for us ! <end>
<start> But that does not mean that we have introduced any morality into the world , just because we have fancied it as obedient . <end>
<start> There are no laws : every power draws its last consequence at every moment . <end>
<start> Things are calculable precisely owing to the fact that there is no possibility of their being otherwise than they are . <end>
<start> effect it produces and the influence it resists . <end>
<start> The anaphoric state which would be thinkable in itself , is entirely Tacking . <end>
<start> It is essentially a will to violence and a will to defend one s self against violence . <end>
<start> It is not self preservation : every atom exercises its influence over the whole of existence it is thought out of existence if one thinks this radio i tion of will power away . <end>
<start> That is why I call it a quantum of Will to Power with this formula one can express the character which cannon be abstracted in thought from mechanical order , without suppressing the latter itself in thought . <end>
<start> The translation of the world of effect into a visible world a world for the eye is the concept movement . <end>
<start> Here it is always understood that I something has been moved , whether it be the fiction of an atomic globule or even of the abstraction of the latter , the dynamic atom , something is always imagined that has an effect that is to say , we have not yet rid ourselves of the habit into which our senses and speech inveigled us . <end>
<start> Subject and object , an agent to the action , the action and that which does it separated : we must not forget that all this signifies no more than semiotics and nothing real . <end>
<start> Mechanics as a teaching of movement is already a translation of phenomena into man s language of the senses . <end>
<start> We are in need of unities in order to be able to reckon : but this is no reason for supposing that unities actually exist . <end>
<start> We borrowed the concept unity from our concept ego , our very oldest article of faith . <end>
<start> If we did not believe ourselves to be unities we should never have formed the concept thing . <end>
<start> Now that is to say , somewhat late in the day , we are overwhelmingly convinced that our conception of the concept ego is no security whatever for a real entity . <end>
<start> In order to maintain the mechanical interpretation of the world theoretically , we must always make the reserve that it is with fictions that we do so : the concept of movement derived from the language of our senses and the concept of the atom entity , derived from our psychical experience are based upon a sense prejudice and a psychological prejudice . <end>
<start> Mechanics formulates consecutive phenomena , and it does so , in the terms of the senses and of the mind that all influence is movement that where there is movement something is at work moving : it does not touch the question of the causal force . <end>
<start> The mechanical world is imagined as the eye and the sense of touch alone could imagine a world as moved , in such a way as to be calculable , as to simulate causal entities things atoms whose effect is constant the transfer of the false concept of subject to the concept atom . <end>
<start> The mixing together of the concept of numbers , of the concept of thing the idea of subject , of the concept of activity the separation of that which is the cause , and the effect , of the concept of movement : all these things are phenomenal our eye and our psychology are still in it all . <end>
<start> over but dynamic quanta , in a relation of tension to all other dynamic quanta : the essence of which resides in their relation to all other quanta , in their influence upon the latter . <end>
<start> The will to power , not Being , not Becoming , but a pathos is the elementary fact , from these first results a Becoming , an influencing . <end>
<start> The physicists believe in a true world after their own kind a fixed of atoms to perform necessary movements , and holding good equally of all creatures , so that , according to them , the world of appearance reduces itself to the side of general and generally needed Being , which is accessible to every one according to his kind accessible and also adjusted , made subjective . <end>
<start> But here they are in error . <end>
<start> The atom which they postulate is arrived at by the logic of that perspective of consciousness it is in itself therefore a subjective fiction . <end>
<start> This picture of the world which they project is in no way essentially different from the subjective picture : the only difference is , that it is composed simply with more extended senses , but certainly with our senses . <end>
<start> And in the end , without knowing it , they left something out of the constellation : precisely the necessary perspective factor by means of which every centre of power and not man alone constructs the rest of the world from its point of view that is to say , measures it , feels it , and moulds it according to its degree of strength . <end>
<start> They forgot to reckon with this perspective power , in true being , or , in school terms , subjecting . <end>
<start> They suppose that this was evolved and added but even the chemical investigator needs it : it is indeed specific Being , which determines action and reaction according to circumstances . <end>
<start> Perspectivity is only a complex form of . <end>
<start> My idea is that every specific body strives to become master of all space , and to extend its fraser its will to power , and to thrust back everything that resists it . <end>
<start> But inasmuch as it is continually meeting the same endeavours on the part of other bodies , it concludes by coming to terms with those by combining with those which are sufficiently related to it and thus they conspire together for power . <end>
<start> And the process continues . <end>
<start> Even in the inorganic world all that concerns an atom of energy is its immediate neighbourhood : distant forces balance each other . <end>
<start> Here is the root of , and it explains why a living organism is egoistic to the core . <end>
<start> Granting that the world disposed of a quantum of force , it is obvious that any transposition of force to any place would affect the whole system thus , besides the causality of sequence , there would also be a dependence , contiguity , and coincidence . <end>
<start> The only possible way of upholding the sense of the concept God would be : to make Him not the motive force , but the condition of maximum power , an epoch a point in the further development of the Will to Power by means of which subsequent evolution just as much as former evolution up to Him could be explained . <end>
<start> Viewed mechanically , the energy of collective Becoming remains constant regarded from the economical standpoint , it ascends to its zenith and then recedes therefrom in order to remain eternally rogatory . <end>
<start> This Will to Power expresses itself in the interpretation , in the manner in which the strength is used . <end>
<start> The conversion of energy into life life in its highest power thenceforward appears as the goal . <end>
<start> The same amount of energy , at different stages of development , means different things . <end>
<start> That which determines growth in Life is the economy which becomes ever more sparing and methodical , which achieves ever more and more with a steadily decreasing amount of energy . <end>
<start> The ideal is the principle of the least possible expense . <end>
<start> The only thing that is proved is that the world is not striving towards a state of stability . <end>

<start> Against Darwinism . <end>

<start> For instance , that which promotes the lasting powers of the individual might be unfavourable to his strength or his beauty that which preserves him might at the same time fix him and keep him stable throughout development . <end>

<start> The influence of environment is nonsensical overrated in Darwin : the essential factor in the process of life is precisely the tremendous inner power to shape and to create forms , which merely uses , exploits environment . <end>
<start> The new forms built up by this inner power are not produced with a view to any end but , in the struggle between the parts , a new form does not exist long without becoming related to some kind of semi utility , and , according to its use , develops itself ever more and more perfectly . <end>
<start> Utility in respect of the acceleration of the speed of evolution , is a different kind of utility from that which is understood to mean the greatest possible stability and staying power of the evolved creature . <end>

<start> The instinct which rules here , must account for this total absence in the organism of a desire to preserve itself : hunger is already an interpretation based upon the observation of a more or less complex organism hunger is a specialised and later form of the instinct it is an expression of the system of divided labour , in the service of a higher instinct which rules the whole . <end>

<start> Pain and pleasure are the most absurd means of expressing judgments , which of course does not mean that the judgments which are enunciated in this way must necessarily be absurd . <end>

<start> My desire would be to see the agent once more identified with the action , after action has been deprived of all meaning by having been separated in thought from the agent I should like to see the notion of doing something , the idea of a purpose , of an intention , of an object , reintroduced into the action , after action has been made insignificant by having been artificially separated from these things . <end>

<start> To have an object , a purpose , or an intention , in fact to will generally , is equivalent to the desire for greater strength , for fuller growth , and for the means thereto in addition . <end>
<start> The most general and fundamental instinct in all action and willing is precisely on that account the one which is least known and is most concealed for in practice we always follow its bidding , for the simple reason that we are in ourselves its bidding . <end>
<start> All valuations are only the results of , and the narrow points of view in serving , this one will : valuing in itself is nothing save this , will to power . <end>
<start> To criticise existence from the standpoint of any one of these values is utter nonsense and error . <end>
<start> Even supposing that a process of annihilation follows from such a value , even so this process is in the service of this will . <end>
<start> The valuation of existence itself ! <end>
<start> But existence is this valuing itself ! <end>
<start> and even when we say no , we still do what we are . <end>
<start> We ought now to perceive the absurdity of this pretence at judging existence and we ought to try and discover what actually takes place there . <end>
<start> It is symptomatic . <end>
<start> Concerning the Origin of our Valuations . <end>
<start> We are able to analyse our body , and by doing so we get the same idea of it as of the stellar system , and the differences between organic and inorganic lapses . <end>
<start> Formerly the movements of the stars were explained as the effects of beings con seriously pursuing a purpose : this is no longer required , and even in regard to the movements of the body and its changes , the belief has long since been abandoned that they can be explained by an appeal to a consciousness which has a determined purpose . <end>
<start> By far the greater number of movements have nothing to do with consciousness at all : neither have they anything ? <end>
<start> ig to do with sensation . <end>
<start> Sensations and thoughts are extremely rare and insignificant things compared with the innumerable phenomena occurring every second . <end>
<start> On the other hand , we believe that a certain conformity of means to ends rules over the very smallest phenomenon , which it is quite beyond our deepest science to understand : a sort of cautiousness , selectiveness , co ordination , and repairing process , etc . <end>
<start> In short , we are in the presence of an activity to which it would be necessary to ascribe an incalculable higher and more extensive intellect than the one we are acquainted with . <end>
<start> We learn to think less of all that is conscious : we unlearn the habit of making ourselves responsible for ourselves , because , as conscious beings fixing purposes , we are but the smallest part of ourselves . <end>
<start> Of the numerous influences taking effect every second , for instance , air , electricity , we feel scarcely anything at all . <end>
<start> There might be a number of forces , which , though they never make themselves felt by us , yet influence us continually . <end>
<start> Pleasure and pain are very rare and scanty phenomena , compared with the countless stimuli with which a cell or an organ operates upon another cell or organ . <end>
<start> It is the phase of the modesty of consciousness . <end>
<start> Finally , we can grasp the conscious ego itself , merely as an instrument in the service of that higher and more extensive intellect : and then we may ask whether all conscious willing , all conscious purposes , all valuations , are not perhaps only means by virtue of which something essentially different is attained , from that which consciousness supposes . <end>
<start> We mean : it is a question of our pleasure and pain but pleasure and pain might be the means whereby we had something to do which lies outside our consciousness . <end>
<start> This is to show how very superficial all conscious phenomena really are how an action and the image of it differ how little we know about what precedes an action how fantastic our feelings , freefall , and cause and effect are how thoughts and images , just like words , are only signs of thoughts the impossibility of finding the grounds of any action the superficiality of all praise and blame how essentially our conscious life is composed of fancies and illusion how all our words merely stand for fancies our emotions too , and how the union of mankind depends upon the transmission and continuation of these fancies : whereas , at bottom , the real union of mankind by means of procreation pursues its unknown way . <end>
<start> Does this belief in the common fancies of men really alter mankind ? <end>
<start> Or is the whole body of ideas and valuations only an expression in itself of unknown changes ? <end>
<start> Are there really such things as will , purposes , thoughts , values ? <end>
<start> Is the whole of conscious life perhaps no more than mirage Even when values seem to determine the actions of a man , they are , as a matter of fact , doing something quite different ! <end>
<start> In short , granting that a certain conformity of means to end might be demonstrated in the action of nature , without the assumption of a ruling ego : could not our notion of purposes , and our will , etc . <end>
<start> be only a symbolic language standing for something quite different that is to say , something and unconscious ? <end>
<start> only the thinnest semblance of that natural conformity of means to end in the organic world , but not in any way different therefrom ? <end>
<start> Briefly , perhaps the whole of mental development is a matter of the body : it is the history of the fact that a higher body is forming . <end>
<start> The organic ascends to higher regions . <end>
<start> Our longing to know Nature is a means by virtue of which the body would reach perfection . <end>
<start> Or , better still , hundreds of thousands of experiments are made to alter the nourishment and the mode of living of the body : the body s consciousness and valuations , its kinds of pleasure and pain , are signs of these changes and experiments . <end>
<start> In the end , it is not a question concerning man for he must be surpassed . <end>
<start> To what Extent are all Interpretations of the World Symptoms of a Ruling Instinct . <end>
<start> The artistic contemplation of the world : to sit before the world and to survey it . <end>
<start> But here the analysis of aesthetic contemplation , its reduction to cruelty , its feeling of security , its judicial and detached attitude , etc . <end>
<start> are lacking . <end>

<start> What instincts does he sublimate ? <end>
<start> The scientific contemplation of the world : a criticism of the psychological longing for science , the desire to make everything comprehensible the desire to make everything practical , useful , capable of being exploited to what extent this is anti aesthetic . <end>

<start> It would be terrible if even history were to be taken possession of in this are here sublimated ! <end>
<start> The religious contemplation of the world : a criticism of the religious man . <end>
<start> It is not necessary to take the moral man as the type , but the man who has extreme feelings of exaltation and of deep depression , and who interprets the former with thankfulness or suspicion without , however , seeking their origin in himself nor the latter either . <end>
<start> The man who essentially feels anything but free , who sublimate his conditions and states of submission . <end>
<start> The moral contemplation of the world . <end>
<start> The feelings peculiar to certain social ranks are projected into the universe : stability , law , the making of things orderly , and the making of things alike , are sought in the highest spheres , because they are valued most highly , above everything or behind everything . <end>
<start> What is common to all : the ruling instincts wish to be regarded as the highest values in general , even as the creative and ruling powers . <end>
<start> It is understood that these instincts either oppose or overcome each other join up synthetically , or alternate in power . <end>
<start> Their profound antagonism is , however , so great , that in those cases in which they all insist upon being gratified , a man of very thorough mediocrity is the outcome . <end>
<start> It is a question whether the origin of our apparent knowledge is not also a mere offshoot of our older valuations , which are so completely assimilated that they belong to the very basis of our nature . <end>
<start> In this way only the more recent needs engage in battle with results of the oldest needs . <end>
<start> The world is seen , felt , and interpreted thus and thus , in order that organic life may be preserved with this particular manner of interpretation . <end>
<start> Man is not only an individual , but the continuation of collective organic life in one definite line . <end>
<start> The fact that man survives , proves that a certain species of interpretations even though it still be added to has also survived that , as a system , this method of interpreting has not changed . <end>
<start> Adaptation . <end>
<start> Our dissatisfaction , our ideal , etc . <end>
<start> may possibly be the result of this incorporated piece of interpretation , of our particular point of view : the organic world may ultimately perish owing to it just as the division of labour in organisms may be the means of bringing about the ruin of the whole , if one part happen to wither or weaken . <end>
<start> The destruction of organic life , and even of the highest form thereof , must follow the same principles as the destruction of the individual . <end>
<start> Judged from the standpoint of the theory of descent , individuation shows the continuous break ing up of one into two , and the equally continuous annihilation of individuals for the sake of a fete individuals , which evolution bears onwards the greater mass always perishes the body . <end>
<start> The fundamental phenomena : innumerable individuals are sacrificed for the sake of a few in order to make the few possible . <end>
<start> One must not allow one s self to be deceived the case is the same with peoples and races : they produce the body for the generation of isolated and valuable individuals who continue the great process am opposed to the theory that the individual studies the interests of the species or of posterity , at the cost of his own advantage : all this is only apparent . <end>
<start> The excessive importance which he attaches to the sexual instinct is not the result of the latter s importance to the species for procreation is the actual performance of the individual , it is his greatest interest , and therefore it is his highest expression of power not judged from the standpoint of consciousness , but from the very centre of the individual . <end>
<start> The fundamental errors of the biologists who have lived hitherto : it is not a matter of the species , but of rearing stronger individuals the many are only a means . <end>
<start> relations to external relations , but will to power , which , proceeding from inside , subjugated and incorporates an ever increasing quantity of external phenomena . <end>
<start> These biologists continue the moral valuations the absolutely higher worth of Altruism , the antagonism towards the lust of dominion , towards war , towards all that which is not useful , and towards all order of rank and of class . <end>
<start> In natural science , the moral depreciation of the ego still goes hand in hand with the overestimation of the species . <end>
<start> But the species is quite as illusory as the ego : a false distinction has been made . <end>
<start> The ego is a hundred times more than a mere unit in a chain of creatures it is the chain itself , in every possible respect and the species is merely an abstraction suggested by the multiplicity and partial similarity of these chains . <end>
<start> That the individual is sacrificed to the species , as people often say he is , is not a fact at all : it is rather only an example of false interpretation . <end>

<start> Anti Darwin . <end>
<start> The domestication of man : what definite value can it have , or has domestication in itself a definite value ? <end>
<start> There are reasons for denying the latter proposition . <end>
<start> Darwin s school of thought certainly goes to great pains to convince us of the reverse : it would fain prove that the influence of domestication may be profound and fundamental . <end>
<start> For the time being , we stand firmly as we did before up to the present no results save very superficial modification or degeneration have been shown to follow upon domestication . <end>
<start> And everything that escapes from the hand and discipline of man , returns almost immediately to its original natural condition . <end>
<start> The type remains constant , man cannon denatured la nature ! <end>
<start> Biologists reckon upon the struggle for existence , the death of the weaker creature and the survival of the most robust , most gifted combatant on that account they imagine a continuous increase in the perfection of all creatures . <end>
<start> We , on the contrary , have convinced ourselves of the fact , that in the struggle for existence , accident serves the cause of the weak quite as much as that of the strong that craziness often supplements strength with advantage that the of a species is related in a remarkable manner to that species chances of destruction . <end>
<start> Natural Selection is also credited with the power of slowly effecting unlimited metamorphoses : it is believed that eVery advantage is transmitted by heredity , and strengthened in the course of generations when heredity is known to be so capricious that . <end>
<start> the happy adaptations of certain creatures to very special conditions of life , are regarded as the result of surrounding influences . <end>
<start> Nowhere , however , are examples of unconscious selection to be found absolutely nowhere . <end>
<start> The most different individuals associate one with the other the extremes become lost in the mass . <end>
<start> Each vies with the other to maintain his kind those creatures whose appearance shields them from certain dangers , do not alter this appearance when they are in an environment quite devoid of danger . <end>
<start> If they live in places where their coats or their hides do not conceal them , they do not adapt themselves to their surroundings in any way . <end>
<start> The selection of the most beautiful has been so exaggerated , that it greatly exceeds the instincts for beauty in our own race ! <end>
<start> As a matter of fact , the most beautiful creature often couples with the most debased , and the largest with the smallest . <end>
<start> We almost always see males and females taking advantage of their first chance meeting , and manifesting no taste or selectiveness at all . <end>
<start> Modification through climate and nourishment but as a matter of fact unimportant . <end>
<start> The growing evolution of creatures is assumed . <end>
<start> All grounds for this assumption are entirely lacking . <end>
<start> Every type has its limitations : beyond these evolution cannon carry it . <end>
<start> My general point of view . <end>
<start> First proposition : Man as a species is not progressing . <end>
<start> Higher specimens are indeed attained but they do not survive . <end>
<start> The general level of the species is not raised . <end>
<start> Second proposition : Man as a species does not represent any sort of progress compared with any other animal . <end>
<start> The whole of the animal and plant world does not develop from the lower to the higher . <end>
<start> but all simultaneously , haphazardly , confusedly , and at variance . <end>
<start> The richest and most complex forms and the term higher type means no more than this perish more easily : only the lowest succeed in maintaining their apparent . <end>
<start> The former are seldom attained , and maintain their superior position with difficulty the latter are compensated by great fruitfulness . <end>
<start> In the human race , also , the superior specimens the happy cases of evolution , are the first to perish amid the fluctuations of chances for and against them . <end>
<start> They are exposed to every form of decadence : they are extreme , and , on that account alone , already decadent . <end>
<start> The short duration of beauty , of genius , of the Caesar , is sui generis : such things are not hereditary . <end>
<start> The type is inherited , there is nothing is not a case of a particular fate , or of the evil will of Nature , but merely of the concept superior type : the higher type is an example of an income parable greater degree of complexity a greater sum of co ordinate elements : but on this account disintegration becomes a thousand times more threatening . <end>
<start> Genius is the sublime machine in existence hence it is the most fragile . <end>
<start> Third proposition : The domestication culture of man does not sink very deep . <end>
<start> When it does sink far below the skin it immediately becomes degeneration type : the Christian . <end>
<start> The wild man or , in moral terminology , the evil man is a reversion to Nature and , in a certain sense , he represents a recovery , a cure from the effects of culture . <end>
<start> Anti Darwin . <end>
<start> What surprises me most on making a general survey of the great destinies of man , is that I invariably see the reverse of what to day Darwin and his school sees or will persist in seeing : selection in favour of the stronger , the better constituted , and the progress of the species . <end>
<start> Precisely the reverse of this stares one in the face : the suppression of the lucky cases , the uselessness of the more highly constituted types , the inevitable mastery of the mediocre , and even of those who are below mediocrity . <end>
<start> Unless we are shown some reason why man is an exception among living creatures , I incline to the belief that Darwin s school is everywhere at fault . <end>
<start> That will to power , in which I perceive the ultimate reason and character of all change , explains why it is that selection is never in favour of the exceptions and of the lucky cases : the strongest and happiest natures are weak when they are confronted with a majority ruled by organised gregarious instincts and the fear which possesses the weak . <end>
<start> My general view of the world of values shows that in the highest values which now sway the destiny of man , the happy cases among men , the select specimens do not prevail : but rather the decadent specimens , perhaps there is nothing more interesting in the world than this unpleasantStrange as it may seem , the strong always have to be upheld against the weak and the against the ill constituted , the healthy against the sick and physiologically botched . <end>
<start> If we drew our morals from reality , they would read thus : the mediocre are more valuable than the mediocre the will to nonentity prevails over the will to life and the general aim now is , in Christian , buddhist , Schopenhauerian phraseology : It is better not to be than to be . <end>
<start> I protest against this formulating of reality into a moral : and I loathe Christianity with a deadly loathing , because it created sublime words and attitudes in order to deck a revolting truth with all the tardiness of justice , virtue , and godliness . <end>
<start> I see all philosophers and the whole of science on their knees before a reality which is the reverse of the struggle for life , as Darwin and his school understood it that is to say , wherever I look , V I see those prevailing and surviving , who throw doubt and suspicion upon life and the value of life . <end>
<start> The error of the Darwinian school became a problem to me : how can one be so blind as to make this mistake ? <end>
<start> That species show an ascending tendency , is the most nonsensical assertion that has ever been made : until now they have only manifested a dead level . <end>
<start> There is nothing whatever to prove that the higher organisms have developed from the lower . <end>
<start> I see that the lower , owing to their numerical strength , their craft , and ruse , now preponderance , and I fail to see an instance in which an accidental change produces an advantage , at least not for a very long period : for it would be necessary to find some reason why an accidental change should become so very strong . <end>
<start> I do indeed find the cruelty of Nature which is so often referred to but in a different place : Nature is cruel , but against her lucky and children she protects and shelters and loves the lowly . <end>
<start> In short , the increase of a species power , as the result of the preponderance of its particularly well constituted and strong specimens , is perhaps less of a certainty than that it is the result of the preponderance of its mediocre and lower specimens . <end>
<start> in the case of the latter , we find great fruitfulness and permanence : in the case of the former , the besetting dangers are greater , waste is more rapid , and decimation is more speedy . <end>
<start> Man as he has appeared up to the present is the embryo of the man of the future all the formative powers which are to produce the latter , already lie in the former : and owing to the fact that they are enormous , the more promising for the future the modern individual happens to be , the more suffering falls to his lot . <end>
<start> This is the profoundest concept of suffering . <end>
<start> The formative powers clash . <end>
<start> The isolation of the individual need not deceive one as a matter of fact , some uninterrupted current does actually flow through all individuals , and does thus unite them . <end>
<start> The fact that they feel themselves isolated , is the most powerful spur in the process of setting themselves the loftiest of aims : their search for happiness is the means which keeps together and moderates the formative powers , and keeps them from being mutually destructive . <end>
<start> Excessive intellectual strength sets itself new goals it is not in the least satisfied by the command and the leadership of the inferior world , or by the preservation of the organism , of the individual . <end>
<start> We are more than the individual : we are the whole chain itself , with the tasks of all the possible futures of that chain in us . <end>
<start> Theory of the Will to Power and of Valuations . <end>
<start> The unitary view of psychology . <end>
<start> We are accustomed to regard the development of a vast number of forms as compatible with one single origin . <end>
<start> My theory would be : that the will to powers the primitive motive force out of which all other motives have been derived That it is exceedingly illuminating to substitute power for individual happiness after which every living organism is said to strive : It strives after power , after more power happiness is only a symptom of the feeling of power attained , a consciousness of difference it does not strive after happiness : but happiness steps in when the object is attained , after which the organism has striven : happiness is an accompanying , not an activating factor That all motive force is the will to power that there is no other force , either physical , dynamic , or psychic . <end>
<start> In our science , where the concept cause and effect is reduced to a relationship of complete equilibrium , and in which it seems desirable for the same quantum of force to be found on either side , all idea of a motive power is absent , we only apprehend results , and we call these equal from the point of view of their content of force . <end>
<start> It is a matter of mere experience that change never ceases : at bottom we have not the smallest grounds for assuming that any one particular change must follow upon any other . <end>
<start> On the contrary , any state which has been attained would seem almost forced to maintain itself intact if it had not within itself a capacity for not desiring to maintain itself . <end>
<start> Spinoza s proposition concerning self preservation ought as a matter of fact to put a stop to change . <end>
<start> But the proposition is false the contrary is true . <end>
<start> In all living organisms it can be clearly shown that they do everything not to remain as they are , but to become greater . <end>
<start> Will to over and causality . <end>
<start> From a psychological point of view the idea of cause is our feeling of power in the act which is called willing our concept effect is the superstition that this feeling of power is itself the force which moves things . <end>
<start> A state which accompanies an event and is already an effect of that event is deemed sufficient cause of the latter the tense relationship of our feeling of power pleasure as the feeling of power and of an obstacle being overcome are these things illusions ? <end>
<start> If we translate the notion cause back into the only sphere which is known to us , and out of which we have taken it , we cannon imagine any change in which the will to power is not inherent . <end>
<start> We do not know how to account for any change which is not a trespassing of one power on another . <end>
<start> Mechanics only show us the results , and then only in images movement is a figure of speech gravitation itself has no mechanical cause , because it is itself the first cause of mechanical results . <end>
<start> The will to accumulate force is confined to the phenomenon of life , to nourishment , to procreation , to inheritance , to society , states , customs , authority . <end>
<start> Should we not be allowed to assume that this will is the motive power also of chemistry ? <end>
<start> and of the cosmic order ? <end>
<start> Not only conservation of energy , but the minimum amount of waste so that the only reality is . <end>
<start> lb . <end>
<start> it this : the will of every centre of power to become stronger not self preservation , but the desire to appropriate , to become master , to become more , to become stronger . <end>
<start> Is the fact that science is possible a proof of the principle of causation From like causes , like effects A permanent law of things Invariable order ? <end>
<start> Because something is calculable , is it therefore on that account necessary ? <end>
<start> If something happens thus , and thus only , it is not the manifestation of a principle , of a law , of order . <end>
<start> What happens is that certain quanta of power begin to operate , and their essence is to exercise their power over all other quanta of power . <end>

<start> e . <end>

<start> All mechanical first principles , matter , atoms , weight , pressure , and repulsion , are not facts in themselves , but interpretations arrived at with the help of psychical fictions . <end>
<start> Life , which is our best known form of being , is altogether will to the accumulation of strength all the processes of life hinge on this : everything aims , not at preservation , but at accretion and accumulation . <end>
<start> Life as an individual case a hypothesis which may be applied to existence in general strives after the maximum feeling of power life is essentially a striving after more power striving itself is only a straining after more power the most fundamental and innermost thing of all is this will . <end>

<start> What is the relation of the whole of the organic process towards the rest of nature ? <end>
<start> Here the J fundamental will reveals itself . <end>
<start> Is the will to power a kind of will , or is it j identical with the concept will ? <end>
<start> Is it equivalent to desiring or commanding is it the will which Schopenhauer says is the essence of things ? <end>
<start> My proposition is that the will of psychologists hitherto has been an unjustifiable generalisation , and that there is no such thing as this sort of will , that instead of the development of one will into several forms being taken as a fact , the character of will has been cancelled owing to the fact that its content , its whither , was subtracted from it : in Schopenhauer this is so in the highest degree what he calls will is merely an empty word . <end>
<start> There is even less plausibility in the will to live : for life is simply one of the manifestations of the will to power it is quite arbitrary and ridiculousftV to suggest that everything is striving to enter into this particular form of the will to power . <end>
<start> If the innermost essence of existence is the will to power if happiness is every increase of power , and unhappiness the feeling of not being able to resist , of not being able to become master : may we not then postulate happiness and pain as cardinal facts ? <end>

<start> But who feels happiness ? <end>
<start> Who will have power ? <end>
<start> Nonsensical question I If the essence of all things is itself will to power , and consequently the ability to feel pleasure and pain ! <end>
<start> Albeit : contrasts and obstacles are necessary , therefore also , relatively , units which trespass on one another . <end>
<start> According to the obstacles which a force seeks with a view of overcoming them , the measure of the failure and the fatality thus provoked must increase : and in so far as every force can only manifest itself against some thing that opposes it , an element of unhappiness is necessarily inherent in every action . <end>
<start> But this pain acts as a greater incitement to life , and increases the will to power . <end>
<start> If pleasure and pain are related to the feeling ot power , life would have to represent such an increase in power that the difference , the plus , would have to enter consciousness . <end>

<start> In a state of decadence after a certain time the opposite difference becomes conscious , that is decrease : the memory of former strong moments depresses the present feelings of happiness in this state comparison reduces happiness . <end>
<start> It is not the satisfaction of the will which is the cause of happiness to this superficial theory I am more particularly opposed this absurd psychological forgery in regard to the most simple things , but it is that the will is always striving to overcome that which stands in its way . <end>
<start> The feeling of happiness lies precisely in the of the will , in the fact that without opponents and obstacles it is never satisfied . <end>
<start> The happy man : a gregarious ideal . <end>
<start> The normal discontent of our instincts for instance , of the instinct of hunger , of sex , of movement contains nothing which is in itself depressing it rather provokes the feeling of life , and , whatever the pessimists may say to us , like all the rhythms of small and irritating stimuli , it strengthens . <end>
<start> Instead of this discontent making us sick of life , it is rather the great stimulus to life . <end>
<start> Pleasure might even perhaps be characterised as the rhythm of small and painful stimuli . <end>
<start> Kant says : These lines of Count verdi s self insole del sincere e del dolores I confirm with absolute certainty : II solo principia motor dell duomo e il dolores . <end>
<start> II dolores precede omni sincere . <end>
<start> II sincere non e un essene positive . <end>
<start> Pain is something different from pleasure I mean it is not the latter s opposite . <end>
<start> If the essence of pleasure has been aptly characterised as the feeling of increased power that is to say , as a feeling of difference which presupposes comparison , that does not define the nature of pain . <end>
<start> The false contrasts which the people , and consequently the language , believes in , are always dangerous fetters which impede the march of truth . <end>
<start> There are even cases where a kind of pleasure is conditioned by a certain rhythmic sequence of small , painful stimuli : in this way a very rapid growth of the feeling of power and of the feeling On the Nature of Pleasure a ? <end>
<start> id Pain . <end>
<start> The only motive force of man is pain . <end>
