<start> Pleasure is not a positive thing . <end>
<start> Tr . <end>
<start> of pleasure is attained . <end>
<start> This is the case , for instance , in tickling , also in the sexual tickling which accompanies the coitus : here we see pain acting as the ingredient of happiness . <end>
<start> It seems to be a small hindrance which is overcome , followed immediately by another small hindrance which once again is overcome this play of resistance and resistance overcome is the greatest exciting of that complete feeling of overflowing and surplus power which constitutes the essence of happiness . <end>
<start> The converse , which would be an increase in the feeling of pain through small intercalated pleasurable stimuli , does not exist : pleasure and pain are not opposites . <end>
<start> Pain is undoubtedly an intellectual process in which a judgment is inherent the judgment harmful , in which long experience is epitomised . <end>
<start> There is no such thing as pain in itself . <end>
<start> It is not the wound that hurts , it is the experience of the harmful results a wound may have for the whole organism , which here speaks in this deeply moving way , and is called pain . <end>
<start> In the case of deleterious influences which were unknown to ancient man , as , for instance , those residing in the new combination of poisonous chemicals , the hint from pain is lacking , and we are lost . <end>
<start> That which is quite peculiar in pain is the prolonged disturbance , the quivering subsequent to a terrible shock in the ganglia of the nervous system . <end>
<start> As a matter of fact , nobody suffers from the cause of pain from any sort of injury , for instance , but from the protracted disturbance of his equilibrium which follows upon the shock . <end>
<start> Pain is a disease of the cerebral centres pleasure is no disease at all . <end>
<start> The fact that pain may be the cause of reflex actions has appearances and even philosophical prejudice in its favour . <end>
<start> But in very sudden accidents , if we observe closely , we find that the reflex action occurs appreciably earlier than the feeling of pain . <end>
<start> I should be in a bad way when I stumbled if I had to wait until the fact had struck the bell of my consciousness , and until a hint of what I had to do had been telegraphed back to me . <end>
<start> On the contrary , what I notice as clearly as possible is , that first , in order to avoid a fall , reflex action on the part of my foot takes place , and then , after a certain measurable space of time , there follows quite suddenly a kind of painful wave in my forehead . <end>
<start> Nobody , then , reacts to pain . <end>
<start> Pain is subsequently projected into the wounded quarter but the essence of this local pain is nevertheless not the expression of a kind of local wound : it is merely a local sign , the strength and nature of which is in keeping with the severity of the wound , and of which the nerve centres have taken note . <end>
<start> The fact that as the result of this shock the muscular power of the organism is materially reduced , does not prove in any way that the essence of pain is to be sought in the lowering of the feeling of power . <end>
<start> Once more let me repeat : nobody reacts to pain : pain is no cause of action . <end>
<start> Pain itself is a reaction the reflex movement is another and earlier process both originate at different points . <end>
<start> The message of pain : in itself pain does not announce that which has been momentarily damaged , but the significance of this damage for the individual as a whole . <end>
<start> Are we to suppose that there are any pains which the species feel , and which the individual does not ? <end>
<start> The sum of unhappiness outweighs the sum . <end>
<start> of happiness : consequently it were better that the I world did not exist The world is something I which from a rational standpoint it were better did not exist , because it occasions more pain than pleasure to the feeling subject this futile gossip now calls itself pessimism ! <end>
<start> Pleasure and pain are accompanying factors , not causes they are second rate valuations derived from a dominating value , they are one with the feeling useful , harmful , and therefore they are absolutely fugitive and relative . <end>
<start> For in regard to all utility and carefulness there are a hundred different ways of asking what for ? <end>
<start> I despise this pessimism of sensitiveness : it is in itself a sign of profoundly impoverished life . <end>
<start> Man does not seek happiness and does not avoid unhappiness . <end>
<start> Everybody knows the famous prejudices I here contradict . <end>
<start> Pleasure and pain are mere results , mere accompanying phenomena that which every man , which every tiny particle of a living organism will have , is an increase of power . <end>
<start> In striving after this , pleasure and pain are encountered it is owing to that will that the organism seeks opposition and requires that which stands in its way . <end>
<start> Pain as the hindrance of its will to power is therefore a normal feature , a natural ingredient of every organic phenomenon man does not avoid it , on the contrary , he is constantly in need of it : every triumph , every feeling of pleasure , every event presupposes an obstacle overcome . <end>
<start> Let us take the simplest case , that of primitive nourishment the protoplasm extends its in order to seek for that which resists it , it does not do so out of hunger , but owing to its will to power . <end>
<start> Then it makes the attempt to overcome , to appropriate , and to incorporate that with which it comes into contact what people call nourishment is merely a derivative , a utilitarian application , of the primordial will to become stronger . <end>
<start> Pain is so far from acting as a diminution of our feeling of power , that it actually forms in the majority of cases a spur to this feeling , the obstacle is the stimulus of the will to power . <end>
<start> Pain has been confounded with one of its subdivisions , which is exhaustion : the latter does indeed represent a profound reduction and lowering of the will to power , a material loss of strength that is to say , there is a pain as the stimulus to an increase or power , and b pain following upon an expenditure of power in the first case it is a spur , in the second it is the outcome of excessive spurring . <end>
<start> The inability to resist is proper to the latter form of pain : the provocation of that which resists is proper to the former . <end>
<start> The only happiness which is to be felt in the state of exhaustion is that of going to sleep in the other case , happiness means triumph . <end>
<start> The great confusion of psychologists consisted in the fact that they did not keep these two kinds of happiness that of falling asleep , and that of triumph sufficiently apart . <end>
<start> Exhausted people will have repose , slackened limbs , peace and quiet and these things constitute the bliss of Nihilistic religions and philosophies the wealthy in vital strength , the active , want triumph , defeated opponents , and the extension of their feeling of power over ever wider regions . <end>
<start> Every healthy function of the organism has this need , and the whole organism constitutes an intricate complexity of systems struggling for the increase of the feeling of power . <end>
<start> How is it that the fundamental article of faith in all psychologies is a piece of most outrageous contortion and fabrication ? <end>
<start> Man strives after happiness , for instance how much of this is true ? <end>
<start> In order to understand what life is , and what kind of striving and tenseness life contains , the formula should hold good not only of trees and plants , but of animals also . <end>
<start> What does the plant strive after ? <end>
<start> But here we have already invented a false entity which does not exist , concealing and denying the fact of an infinitely variegated growth , with individual and semi individual starting points , if we give it the clumsy title plant as if it were a unit . <end>
<start> It is very obvious that the ultimate and smallest individuals cannon be understood in the sense of metaphysical individuals or atoms their sphere of power is continually shifting its ground : but with all these changes , can it be said that any of them strives after happiness ? <end>
<start> All this expanding , this incorporation and growth , is a search for resistance movement is essentially related to states of pain : the driving power here must represent some other desire if it . <end>
<start> leads to such continual willing and seeking of pain . <end>
<start> To what end do the trees of a virgin forest contend with each other ? <end>
<start> For happiness ? <end>
<start> For power ! <end>
<start> Man is now master of the forces of nature , and master too of his own wild and unbridled feelings the passions have followed suit , and have learned to become useful in comparison with primeval man , the man of to day represents an enormous quantum of power , but not an increase in happiness ! <end>
<start> How can one maintain , then , that he has striven after happiness ? <end>
<start> But while I say this I see above me , and below the stars , the glittering rat s tail of errors which hitherto has represented the greatest inspiration of man : All happiness is the result of virtue all virtue is the result of free will ! <end>
<start> Let us the values : all capacity is the outcome of a happy organisation , all freedom is the outcome of capacity freedom understood here as facility in self direction . <end>
<start> Every artist will understand me . <end>
<start> The value of life . <end>
<start> Every life stands by itself all existence must be justified , and not only life , the justifying principle must be one through which life itself speaks . <end>
<start> Life is only a means to something : it is the expression of the forms of growth in power . <end>
<start> The conscious world cannon be a starting-point for valuing : an objective valuation is necessary . <end>
<start> In comparison with the enormous and comply J acted antagonistic processes which the collective life of every organism represents , its conscious world of feelings , intentions , and valuations , is only a small slice . <end>
<start> We have absolutely no right to postulate this particle of consciousness as the object , the wherefore , of the collective phenomena of life : the attainment of consciousness is obviously only an additional means to the unfolding of life and to the extension of its power . <end>
<start> That is why it is a piece of childish simplicity to set up happiness , or intellectuality , or morality , or any other individual sphere of consciousness , as the highest value : and maybe to justify the world with it . <end>
<start> This is my fundamental objection to all philosophical and moral cosmologies and theologies , to all wherefores and highest values that have appeared in philosophies and philosophic religions hitherto . <end>
<start> A kind of means is misunderstood as the object itself : conversely life and its growth of power were debased to a means . <end>
<start> If we wished to postulate an adequate object of life it would not necessarily be related in any way with the category of conscious life it would require rather to explain conscious life as a mere means to itself . <end>
<start> The denial of life regarded as the object of life , the object of evolution ! <end>
<start> Existence a piece of tremendous stupidity ! <end>
<start> Any such mad interpretation is only the outcome of life s being measured by the factors of consciousness pleasure and pain , good and evil . <end>
<start> Here the means are made to stand against the end the unholy , absurd , and , above all , disagreeable means : how can the end be any use when it requires such means ? <end>
<start> But where the fault lies is here instead of looking for the end which would explain the necessity of such means , we posited an end from the start which actually excludes such means , i . <end>
<start> e . <end>
<start> we made a desideratum in regard to certain means especially pleasurable , rational , and virtuous into a rule , and then only did we decide what end would be desirable . <end>
<start> Where the fundamental fault lies is in the fact that , instead of regarding consciousness as an instrument and an isolated phenomenon of life in general , we made it a standard , the highest value in life : it is the faulty standpoint of a parte ad totem , and that is why all philosophers are instinctively seeking at the present day for a collective consciousness , a thing that lives and wills consciously with all that happens , a Spirit , a God . <end>
<start> But they must be told that it is precisely thus that life is converted into a monster that a God and a general tentorium would necessarily be something on whose account the whole of existence would have to be condemned . <end>
<start> Our greatest relief came when we eliminated the general consciousness which postulates ends and means in this way we ceased from being necessarily pessimists . <end>
<start> Our greatest indictment of life was the existence of God . <end>
<start> Concerning the value of Becoming . <end>
<start> If the movement of the world really tended to reach a final state , that state would already have been reached . <end>
<start> The only fundamental fact , however , is that it does not tend to reach a final state : and every philosophy and scientific hypothesis eg . <end>
<start> materialism according to which such a final state is necessary , is refuted by this fundamental fact . <end>
<start> I should like to have a concept of the world which does justice to this fact . <end>
<start> Becoming ought to be explained without having recourse to such final designs . <end>
<start> Becoming must appear justified at every instant or it must defy all valuation : which has unity as its end the present must not under any circumstances be justified by a future , nor must the past be justified for the sake of represent . <end>
<start> Necessity must not be interpreted in the form of a prevailing and ruling collective force or as a prime motor and still less as the necessary cause of some valuable result . <end>
<start> But to this end it is necessary to deny a collective consciousness for Becoming , a God , in order that life may not be veiled under the shadow of a being who feels and knows as we do and yet wills nothing : God is useless if he wants nothing and if he do want something , this presupposes a general sum of suffering and irrationality which lowers the general value of Becoming . <end>
<start> Fortunately any such general power is lacking a suffering God overlooking everything , a general tentorium and ubiquitous Spirit , would be the greatest indictment of existence . <end>
<start> Strictly speaking nothing of the nature of Being must be allowed to remain , because in that case Becoming loses its value and gets to be sheer and superfluous nonsense . <end>
<start> The next question , then , is : how did the illusion Being originate why was it obliged to originate Likewise : how was it that all valuations based upon the hypothesis that there was such a thing as Being came to be depreciated . <end>
<start> But in this way we have recognised that this hypothesis concerning Being is the source of all the calumny that has been directed against the world the Better world , the True world the World Beyond , the Thing in itself . <end>
<start> i Becoming has no final state , it does not tend towards stability . <end>
<start> the world of Being is probably . <end>
<start> at every instant the sum of its value always remains equal : expressed otherwise , it has no value for that according to which it might be measured , and ii regard to which the word value might have some sense , is entirely lacking . <end>
<start> The collective value of the world defies valuation for this reason philosophical pessimism belongs to the order of farces . <end>
<start> We should not make our little desiderata the judges of existence ! <end>
<start> Neither should we make culminating evolutionary forms e . <end>
<start> g . <end>
<start> mind the absolute which stands behind evolution ! <end>
<start> Our knowledge has become scientific to the extent in which it has been able to make use of number and measure . <end>
<start> It might be worth while to try and see whether a scientific order of values might not be constructed according to a scale of numbers and measures representing energy . <end>
<start> All other values are matters of prejudice , simplicity , and misunderstanding . <end>
<start> They may all be reduced to that scale of numbers and measures representing energy . <end>
<start> The ascent in this scale would represent an increase of value , the descent a diminution . <end>
<start> But here appearance and prejudice are against one moral values are only apparent values compared with those which are physiological . <end>
<start> Why the standpoint of value lapses : Because in the whole process of the universe the work of mankind does not come under consideration because a general process viewed in the light of a system does not exist . <end>
<start> Because there is no such thing as a whole because no depreciation of human existence or human aims can be made in regard to something that does not exist . <end>
<start> Because necessity , causality , design , are merely useful semblance . <end>
<start> Because the aim is not the increase of the sphere of consciousness , but the increase of power in which increase the utility of consciousness is also contained and the same holds good of pleasure and pain . <end>
<start> Because a mere means must not be elevated to the highest criterion of value such as states of consciousness like pleasure and pain , if consciousness is in itself only a means . <end>
<start> Because the world is not an organism at all , but a thing of chaos because the development of intellectuality is only a means tending relatively I to extend the duration of an organisation . <end>
<start> Because all desirability has no sense in regard to the general character of existence . <end>
<start> God is the culminating moment : life is an eternal process of defying and unedifying . <end>
<start> But withal there is no zenith of values , but only a zenith of power . <end>
<start> Absolute exclusion of mechanical and materialistic interpretations : they are both only expressions of inferior states , of emotions deprived of all spirit of the will to power . <end>
<start> The retrograde movement from the zenith of development the intellectualisation of power on some slave infected soil may be shown to be the result of the highest degree of energy turning against itself , once it no longer has anything to organise , and utilising its power in order to disorganised . <end>
<start> a The ever increasing suppression of societies , and the latter s subjection by a smaller number of stronger individuals . <end>
<start> b The ever increasing suppression of the privileged and the strong , hence the rise of democracy , and ultimately of anarchy , in the elements . <end>
<start> Value is the highest amount of power that a man can assimilate a man , not mankind ! <end>
<start> Man kind is much more of a means than an end . <end>
<start> It is a question of type : mankind is merely the experimental material it is the overflow of the I ill constituted a field of ruins . <end>
<start> I Words relating to values are merely banners planted on those spots where a new blessedness was discovered a new feeling . <end>
<start> The standpoint of value is the same as that of the conditions of preservation and enhancement , in regard to complex creatures of relative stability appearing in the course of evolution . <end>
<start> There are no such things as lasting and ultimate entities , no atoms , no monads : here also permanence was first introduced by ourselves from practical , utilitarian , and other motives . <end>
<start> The forms that rule the sphere of the subjugated is continually extended or it decreases or increases according to the conditions nourishment being either favourable or unfavourable . <end>
<start> Value is essentially the standpoint for the increase or decrease of these dominating centres in any case for unity cannon be observed anywhere in the nature of development . <end>
<start> The means of expression afforded by language are useless for the purpose of conveying any facts concerning development : the need of positing a rougher world of stable existences and things forms part of our eternal desire for pi reservation . <end>
<start> We may speak of atoms and monads in a relative sense : and this is certain , that the smallest world is the most stable world . <end>
<start> There is no such thing as will : there are only punctuation of will , which are constantly increasing and decreasing their power . <end>
<start> III . <end>
<start> THE WILL TO POWER AS EXEMPLIFIED IN SOCIETY AND THE INDIVIDUAL . <end>
<start> i . <end>
<start> Society and the State . <end>
<start> WE take it as a principle that only individuals feel any responsibility . <end>
<start> Corporations are invented to do what the individual has not the courage to do . <end>
<start> For this reason all communities are vastly more upright and instructive , as regards the nature of man , than the individual who is too cowardly to have the courage of his own desires . <end>
<start> All altruism is the prudence of the private man : societies are not mutually altruistic . <end>
<start> The commandment , Thou shalt love thy next door neighbour , has never been extended to thy neighbour in general . <end>
<start> Rather what Manu says is probably truer : We must conceive of all the States on our own frontier , and their allies , as being hostile , and for the same reason we must consider all of their neighbours as being friendly to us . <end>
<start> The study of society is invaluable , because man in society is far more childlike than man in K individually . <end>
<start> Society has never regarded virtue as anything else than as a means to strength , power , and order . <end>
<start> Manu s words again are simple and dignified : Virtue could hardly rely on her own strength alone . <end>
<start> Really it is only the fear of punishment that keeps men in their limits , and leaves every one in peaceful possession of his own . <end>
<start> The State , or morality organised , is from within the police , the penal code , status , commerce , and the family and from without , the will to war , to power , to conquest and revenge . <end>
<start> A multitude will do things an individual will not , because of the division of responsibility , of command and execution because the virtues of obedience , duty , patriotism , and local sentiment are all introduced because feelings of pride , severity , strength , hate , and revenge in short , all typical traits are upheld , and these are characteristics utterly alien to the herd man . <end>
<start> You haven t , any of you , the courage either to kill or to flog a man . <end>
<start> But the huge machinery of the State quell the individual and makes him decline to be answerable for his own deed obedience , loyalty , etc . <end>
<start> Everything that a man does in the service of the State is against his own nature . <end>
<start> Similarly , everything he learns in view of future service of the State . <end>
<start> This result is obtained through division of labour so that responsibility is subdivided too : The teacher of discipline and those who have grown hard and severe under discipline . <end>
<start> A division of labour among the emotions exists inside society , making individuals and classes produce an imperfect , but more useful , kind of soul . <end>
<start> Observe how every type in society has become atrophied with regard to certain emotions with the view of fostering and accentuating other emotions . <end>
<start> Economically , as aiming at the greatest possible use of all individual power , with the view of preventing the waste of exceptional natures . <end>
<start> aesthetically , as the formation of fixed types , and the pleasure in one s own . <end>
<start> Politically , as the art of bearing with the severe divergencies of the degrees of power in society . <end>
<start> Psychologically , as an imaginary preference for the bungled and the mediocre , in order to preserve the weak . <end>
<start> Man has one terrible and fundamental wish he desires power , and this impulse , which is called freedom , must be the longest restrained . <end>
<start> Hence ethics has instinctively aimed at such an education as shall restrain the desire for power thus our morality slanders the would be tyrant , and glorifies charity , patriotism , and the ambition of the herd . <end>
<start> Impotence to power , how it disguises itself and plays the hypocrite , as obedience , subordination , the pride of duty and morality , submission , devotion , love the ionisation and apotheosis of the commander is a kind of compensation , and indirect self enhancement . <end>
<start> It veils itself further under fatalism and resignation , objectivity , , stoicism , asceticism , self abnegation , allowing . <end>
<start> Other disguises are : criticism , pessimism , indignation , susceptibility , beautiful soul , virtue , self deification , philosophic detachment , freedom from contact with the world the realisation of impotence disguises itself as disdain . <end>
<start> There is a universal need to exercise some kind of power , or to create for one s self the appearance of some power , if only temporarily , in the form of intoxication . <end>
<start> There are men who desire power simply for the sake of the happiness it will bring these belong chiefly to political parties . <end>
<start> Other men have the same yearning , even when power means visible disadvantages , the sacrifice of their happiness , and well being they are the ambitious . <end>
<start> Other men , again , are only like dogs in a manger , and will have i power only to prevent its falling into the hands of others on whom they would then be dependent . <end>
<start> If there be justice and equality before the law , what would thereby be abolished ? <end>
<start> Suspense , enmity , hatred . <end>
<start> But it is a mistake to think that you thereby increase happiness for the corsican rejoice in more happiness than the Continentals . <end>
<start> Reciprocity and the expectation of a reward is one of the most seductive forms of the devaluation of mankind . <end>
<start> It involves that equality which depreciated any gulf as immoral . <end>
<start> Utility is entirely dependent upon the object to be attained , the wherefore ? <end>
<start> And this wherefore , this purpose , is again dependent upon the degree of power . <end>
<start> Utilitarianism is not , therefore , a fundamental doctrine it is only a story of sequels , and cannon be made obligatory for all . <end>
<start> Of old , the State was regarded theoretically as a utilitarian institution it has now become so in a practical sense . <end>
<start> The time of kings has gone by , because people are no longer worthy of them . <end>
<start> They do not wish to see the symbol of their ideal in a king , but only a means to their own ends . <end>
<start> That s the whole truth . <end>
<start> lI am trying to grasp the absolute sense of the communal standard of judgment and valuation , naturally without any intention of deducing morals . <end>
<start> The degree of psychological falsity and tenseness required in order to sanctify the emotions essential to preservation and expansion of power , y and to create a good conscience for them . <end>
<start> The degree of stupidity required in order that general rules and values may remain possible including education , formation of culture , and training . <end>
<start> The degree of inquisitiveness , suspicion , and intolerance required in order to deal with exceptions , to suppress them as criminals , and thus to give them bad consciences , and to make them sick with their own singularity . <end>
<start> Morality is essentially a shield , a means of defence and , in so far , it is a sign of the imperfectly developed man he is still in armour he is still stoical . <end>
<start> The fully developed man is above all provided with weapons : he is a man who attacks . <end>
<start> The weapons of war are converted into weapons of peace out of scales and carapaces grow feathers and hair . <end>
<start> The very notion , living organism , implies that there must be growth , that there must be a striving after an extension of power , and therefore a process of absorption of other forces . <end>
<start> Under the drowsiness brought on by moral narcotics , people speak of the right of the individual to defend himself on the same principle one might speak of his right to attack : for both and the latter more than the former are necessities where all living organisms are concerned : aggressive and defensive egoism are not questions of choice or even of free will , but they are fatalities of life itself . <end>
<start> In this respect it is immaterial whether one have an individual , a living body , or an advancing society in view . <end>
<start> The right to punish or society s means of defence has been arrived at only through a misuse of the word right : a right is acquired only by contract , but self-defence and self preservation do not stand upon the basis of a contract . <end>
<start> A people ought at least , with quite as much justification , to be able to regard its lust of power , either in arms , commerce , trade , or colonisation , as a right the right of growth , perhaps . <end>
<start> When the instincts of a society ultimately make it give up war and renounce conquest , it is decadent : it is ripe for democracy and the rule of shopkeepers . <end>
<start> In the majority of cases , it is true , assurances of peace are merely stupefyingly draughts . <end>
<start> The maintenance of the military State is the last means of adhering to the great tradition of the past or , where it has been lost , to revive it . <end>
<start> By means of it the superior or strong type of man is preserved , and all institutions and ideas which perpetuate enmity and order of rank in States , such as national feeling , protective tariffs , etc . <end>
<start> may on that account seem justified . <end>
<start> In order that a thing may last longer than a person that is to say , in order that a work may outlive the individual who has created it , all manner of limitations and prejudices must be imposed upon people . <end>
<start> But how ? <end>
<start> By means of love , reverence , gratitude towards the person who created the work , or by means of the thought that our ancestors fought for it , or by virtue of the feeling that the safety of our descendants will be secured if we uphold the work for instance , the polls . <end>
<start> Morality is essentially the means of making something survive the individual , because it makes him of necessity a slave . <end>
<start> Obviously the aspect from above is different from the aspect from below , and will lead to quite different interpretations . <end>
<start> How is organised power maintained By the fact that countless generations sacrifice themselves to its cause . <end>
<start> Marriage , property , speech , tradition , race , family , people , and State , are each links in a chain separate parts which have a more or less high or low origin . <end>
<start> Economically they are justified by the surplus derived from the advantages of uninterrupted work and multiple production , as weighed against the disadvantages of greater expense in barter and the difficulty of making things last . <end>
<start> The working parts are multiplied , and yet remain largely idle . <end>
<start> Hence the cost of producing them is greater , and the cost of maintaining them by no means inconsiderable . <end>
<start> The advantage consists in avoiding interruption and incident loss . <end>
<start> Nothing is more expensive than a start . <end>
<start> The higher the standard of living , the greater will be the expense of maintenance , nourishment , and propagation , as also the risk and the probability of an utter fall on reaching the summit . <end>
<start> In bourgeois marriages , naturally in the best sense of the word marriage , there is no question whatsoever of love any more than there is of money . <end>
<start> For on love no institution can be founded . <end>
<start> The whole matter consists in society giving leave to two persons to satisfy their sexual desires under conditions obviously designed to safeguard social order . <end>
<start> Of course there must be a certain attraction between the parties and a vast amount of good nature , patience , compatibility , and charity in any such contract . <end>
<start> But the word love should not be misused as regards such . <end>
<start> y a union . <end>
<start> For two lovers , in the real and strong meaning of the word , the satisfaction of sexual desire is inessential it is a mere symbol . <end>
<start> For the one side , as I have already said , it is a symbol of unqualified submission : for the other , a sign of condescension a sign of the appropriation of property . <end>
<start> Marriage , as understood by the real old nobility , meant the breeding forth of the race but are there any nobles nowadays ? <end>
<start> Quceritur , that is to say , the maintenance of a fixed definite type of ruler , for which object husband and wife were sacrificed . <end>
<start> Naturally the first consideration here had nothing to do with love on the contrary ! <end>
<start> It did not even presuppose that mutual sympathy which is the sine qua non of the bourgeois marriage . <end>
<start> The prime consideration was the interest of the race , and in the second place came the interest of a particular class . <end>
<start> But in the face of the coldness and rigour and calculating lucidity of such a noble concept of marriage as prevailed among every healthy aristocracy , like that of ancient Athens , and even of Europe during the eighteenth century , we warm blooded animals , with our miserably oversensitive hearts , we moderns , cannon restrain a slight shudder . <end>
<start> That is why love as a passion , in the big meaning of this word , was invented for , and in , an aristocratic community where convention and abstinence are most severe . <end>
<start> Concerning the future of marriage . <end>
<start> A superstar on inherited property , a longer term of military service for bachelors of a certain minimum age within the community . <end>
<start> Privileges of all sorts for fathers who lavish boys upon the world , and perhaps plural votes as well . <end>
<start> A medical certificate as a condition of any marriage , endorsed by the parochial authorities , in which a series of questions addressed to the parties and the medical officers must be answered family histories . <end>
<start> As a counter agent to prostitution , or as its ennoblement , I would recommend leasehold marriages to last for a term of years or months , with adequate provision for the children . <end>
<start> Every marriage to be warranted and sanctioned by a certain number of good men and true , of the parish , as a parochial obligation . <end>
<start> Another commandment of philanthropy . <end>
<start> There are cases where to have a child would be a crime for example , for chronic invalids and extreme . <end>
<start> These people should be converted to chastity , and for this purpose the music of L Parsifal might at all events be tried . <end>

<start> Lastly , society here has a positive duty to fulfil , and of all the demands that are made on it , there are few and necessary than this one . <end>
<start> Society as the trustee of life , is responsible to life for every botched life that comes into existence , and as it has to atone for such lives , it ought consequently to make it impossible for them ever to see the light , of day : it should in many cases actually prevent the act of procreation , and may , without any regard for rank , descent , or intellect , hold in readiness the most rigorous forms of compulsion and restriction , and , under certain circumstances , have recourse to castration . <end>
<start> The Mosaic law , Thou shalt do no murder , is a piece of ingenuous sterility compared with the earnestness of this forbidding of life to decadent , Thou shalt not beget ! <end>
<start> For life itself recognises no solidarity or equality of rights between the healthy and unhealthy parts of an organism . <end>

<start> Compassion for decadent , equal rights for the physiologically botched this would be the very pinnacle of immorality , it would be setting up Nature s most formidable opponent as morality itself ! <end>
<start> There are some delicate and morbid natures , the so called idealists , who can never under any circumstances rise above a coarse , immature crime : yet it is the great justification of their anaemic little existence , it is the small recital for their lives of cowardice and falsehood to have been for one instant at least strong . <end>
<start> But they generally collapse after such an act . <end>
<start> In our civilised world we seldom hear of any but the bloodless , trembling criminal , overwhelmed by the curse and contempt of society , doubting even himself , and always belittling and belying his deeds a misbegotten sort of criminal that is why we are opposed to the idea that all great men have been criminals only in the grand style , and neither petty nor pitiful , that crime must be inherent in greatness this at any rate is the unanimous verdict of all those students of human nature who have sounded the deepest waters of great souls . <end>

<start> In times when man is led by reward and punishment , the class of man which the legislator has in view is still of a low and primitive type : he is treated as one treats a child . <end>
<start> In our latterday culture , general degeneracy removes all sense from reward and punishment . <end>
<start> This determination of action by the prospect of reward and punishment presupposes young , strong , and vigorous races . <end>

<start> The effect of prohibition . <end>
<start> Every power which forbids and which knows how to excite fear in the person forbidden creates a guilty conscience . <end>
<start> That is to say , a person has a certain desire but is conscious of the danger of gratifying it , and is consequently forced to be secretive , underhand , and cautious . <end>
<start> Thus any prohibition deteriorates the character of those who do not willingly submit themselves to it , but are constrained thereto . <end>

<start> Dostoievsky was not far wrong when he said of the inmates of the penal colonies in Siberia , that they constituted the strongest and most valuable portion of the Russian people . <end>

<start> The Atonement of all Sin . <end>
<start> People speak of the profound injustice of the social arrangement , as if the fact that one man is born in favourable circumstances and that another is born in unfavourable ones or that one should possess gifts the other has not , were on the face of it an injustice . <end>

<start> The fact that such a theory no longer meets with understanding or rather , let us say , contempt is accounted for by that particle of Christianity which still circulates in the blood of every one of us it makes us tolerant towards things simply because we scent a Christian savour about them . <end>
<start> The Socialists appeal to the Christian instincts this is their really refined piece of cleverness . <end>
<start> Thanks to Christianity , we have now grown accustomed to the superstitious concept of a soul of an immortal soul , of soul monads , which , as a matter of fact , hails from somewhere else , and which has only become inherent in certain cases that is to say , become incarnate in them by accident : but the nature of these cases is not altered , let alone determined by it . <end>
<start> The circumstances of society , of relationship , and of history are only accidents for the soul , perhaps misadventures : in any case , the world is not their work . <end>

<start> that is to say , politically , , risen to pessimistically . <end>
<start> Wherever responsible circumstances or people have been looked for , it was the instinct of revenge that sought them . <end>
<start> This instinct of revenge obtained such an ascendancy over man in the course of centuries that the whole of metaphysics , psychology , ideas of society , and , above all , morality , are tainted with it . <end>
<start> Man has nourished this idea of responsibility to such an extent that he has introduced the bacillus of vengeance into everything . <end>
<start> By means of it he has made God Himself ill , and killed innocence in the universe , by tracing every condition of things to acts of will , to intentions , to responsible agents . <end>
<start> The whole teaching of will , this most fatal fraud that has ever existed in psychology hitherto , was invented essentially for the purpose of punishment . <end>
<start> It was the social utility of punishment that lent this concept its dignity , its power , and its truth . <end>
<start> The originator of that psychology , that we shall call vocational psychology , must be sought in those classes which had the right of punishment in their hands above all , therefore , among the priests who stood on the very pinnacle of ancient social systems : these people wanted to create for themselves the right to wreak revenge they wanted to supply God with the privilege of vengeance . <end>
<start> For this purpose man was declared free : to this end every action had to be regarded as voluntary , and the origin of every deed had to be considered as lying in consciousness . <end>
<start> But by such propositions as these ancient psychology is refuted . <end>
<start> To day , when Europe seems to have taken the contrary direction when we would fain withdraw , dissipate , and banish the concept of guilt and punishment with all our might from the world when our most serious endeavours are concentrated upon purifying psychology , morality , history , nature , social institutions and privileges , and even God Himself , from this filth in whom must we recognise our most mortal enemies ? <end>
<start> Precisely in those apostles of revenge and resentment , in those who are par excellence pessimists from indignation , who make it their mission to sanctify their filth with the name of righteous indignation . <end>
<start> We others , whose one desire is to reclaim innocence on behalf of Becoming , would fain be the missionaries of a purer thought , namely , that no one is responsible for man s qualities neither God , nor society , nor his parents , nor his ancestors , nor himself in fact , that no one is to blame for him . <end>
<start> The being who might be made responsible for a man s existence , for the fact that he is constituted in a particular way , or for his birth in certain circumstances and in a certain environment , is absolutely lacking . <end>
<start> And it is a great blessing that such a being is non existent . <end>
<start> We are not the result of an eternal design , of a will , of a desire : there is no attempt being made with us to attain to an ideal of perfection , to an ideal of happiness , to an ideal of virtue , and we are just as little the result of a mistake on God s part in the presence of which He ought to feel uneasy a thought which is known to be at the very root of the Old Testament . <end>
<start> There is not a place nor a purpose nor a sense to which we can attribute our existence or our kind of existence . <end>
<start> In the first place , no one is in a position to do this : it is quite impossible to judge , to measure , or to compare , or even to deny the whole universe ! <end>
<start> And why ? <end>
<start> For five reasons , all accessible to the man of average intelligence : for instance , because there is no existence outside the universe . <end>

<start> Fundamental errors : to regard the herd as an aim instead of the individual ! <end>

<start> The increasing humanity of this tendency consists in the fact that we are beginning to feel ever more subtly how difficult it is really to absorb others : while we could show our power by injuring him , his will estranged him from us , and thus makes him less susceptible of being overcome . <end>
<start> The degree of resistance which has to be continually overcome in order to remain at the top , is the measure of freedom , whether for individuals or for societies : freedom being understood as positive power , as will to power . <end>

<start> A criticism of selfishness . <end>

<start> Individualism is a modest and still unconscious form of will to power with it a single human unit seems to think it sufficient to free himself from the power of society or of the State or Church . <end>

<start> The History of mobilisation and Demoralisation . <end>
<start> Proposition one . <end>
<start> There are no such things as moral actions : they are purely imaginary . <end>
<start> Not only is it impossible to demonstrate their existence a fact which Kant and Christianity , for instance , both acknowledged but they are not even possible . <end>
<start> Owing to psychological misunderstanding , a man invented an opposite to the instinctive impulses of life , and believed that a new species of instinct was thereby discovered : a primus mobile was postulated which does not exist at all . <end>
<start> According to the valuation which gave rise to the antithesis moral and immoral , one should say : There is nothing else on earth but immoral intentions and actions . <end>
<start> Proposition two . <end>
<start> The whole differentiation , moral and immoral , arises from the assumption that both moral and immoral actions are the result of a spontaneous will in short , that such , a will exists or in other words , that moral judge meets can only hold good with regard to intuitions and actions that are free . <end>
<start> But this whole order of actions and intentions is purely imaginary : the only world to which the moral standard could be applied does not exist at all : there is no such thing as a moral or an immoral action . <end>
<start> The psychological error out of which the antithesis moral and immoral arose is : selfless , unselfish , self denying all unreal and fantastic . <end>
<start> A false dogmatism also clustered around the concept ego it was regarded as atomic , and falsely opposed to a non ego it was also liberated north were from Becoming , and declared to belong to the sphere of Being . <end>
<start> The false materialization of the ego : this owing to the belief in individual immortality was made an article of faith under the pressure of religion moral discipline . <end>
<start> According to his artificial liberation of the ego and its transference to the realm of the absolute , people thought that they had arrived at an antithesis in values which seemed quite irrefutable the single ego and the vast non ego . <end>
<start> It seemed obvious that the value of the individual ego could only exist in conjunction with the vast non ego , more particularly in the sense of being subject to it and existing only for its sake . <end>
<start> Here , of course , the gregarious instinct determined the direction of thought : nothing is more opposed to this instinct than the sovereignty of the individual Supposing , however , that the ego be absolute , then its value must lie in self negation . <end>
<start> The gregarious self conceit which abhors the desire to remain an atom , and regards it as hostile . <end>
<start> As a result : the overcoming of the individual by changing his aim . <end>
<start> At this point there appeared to be actions that were self facing : around these actions a whole sphere of antitheses was fancied . <end>
<start> It was asked , in what sort of actions does man most strongly assert himself ? <end>

<start> etc . <end>

<start> Hitherto there has been no German culture . <end>
<start> It is no refutation of this assertion to say that there have been great anchor rites in Germany Goethe , for instance for these had their own culture . <end>

<start> German culture was a thing devoid of character and of almost unlimited yielding power . <end>

<start> I distinguish between courage before persons , courage before things , and courage on paper . <end>

<start> Romanticism and its opposite . <end>
<start> In regard to all aesthetic values I now avail myself of this fundamental distinction : in every individual case I ask myself has hunger or has superabundance been creative here ? <end>
<start> At first another distinction might perhaps seem preferable , it is far more obvious , e . <end>
<start> g . <end>
<start> the distinction which decides whether a desire for stability , for eternity , for Being , or whether a desire for destruction , for change , for Becoming , has been the cause of creation . <end>
<start> But both kinds of desire , when examined more closely , prove to be ambiguous , and really susceptible of interpretation only according to that scheme already mentioned and which I think is rightly preferred . <end>
<start> The desire for destruction , for change , for Becoming , may be the expression of an overflowing power pregnant with promises for the future my term for this , as is well known , is Dionysian it may , however , also be the hate of the ill constituted , of the needy and of the physiologically botched , that destroys , and must destroy , because such creatures are indignant at , and annoyed by everything lasting and stable . <end>
<start> The act of can , on the other hand , be the outcome of gratitude and love : an art which has this origin is always an apotheosis art dithyramb , as perhaps with Rubens happy , as perhaps with Hafiz bright and gracious , and shedding a ray of glory over all things , as in Goethe . <end>
<start> But it may also , however , be the outcome of the tyrannical will of the great sufferer who would make the most personal , individual , and narrow trait about him , the actual idiosyncrasy of his pain in fact , into a binding law and imposition , and who thus wreaks his revenge upon all things by stamping , branding , and violating them with the image of his torment . <end>
<start> The latter case is romantic pessimism in its highest form , whether this be Schopenhauerian voluntarism or Wagnerian music . <end>
<start> It is a question whether the antithesis , classic and romantic , does not conceal that other antithesis , the active and the reactive . <end>
<start> THE WILL TO POWER . <end>
<start> In order to be a classic , one must be possessed of all the strong and apparently contradictory gifts and passions : but in such a way that they run in harness together , and culminate simultaneously in elevating a certain species of literature or art or politics to its height and zenith they must not do this after that elevation has taken place . <end>
<start> They must reflect the complete state either of a people or of a culture , and express its most profound and most secret nature , at a time when it is still stable and not yet discoloured by the imitation of foreign things or when it is still dependent . <end>
<start> not a reactive but a deliberate and progressive spirit , saying Yea in all circumstances , even in its hate . <end>
<start> And does not the highest personal value belong thereto ? <end>
<start> It is worth considering whether moral prejudices do not perhaps exercise their influence here , and whether great moral loftiness is not perhaps a contradiction of the classical ? <end>
<start> Whether the moral monsters must not necessarily be romantic in word and deed ? <end>
<start> Any such preponderance of one virtue over others as in the case of the moral monster is precisely what with most hostility counteracts the classical power in equilibrium supposing a people manifested this moral loftiness and were classical notwithstanding , we should have to conclude boldly that they were also on the same high level in immorality ! <end>
<start> this was perhaps the case with Shakespeare provided that he was really Lord Bacon . <end>
<start> Concerning the future . <end>
<start> Against the romanticism of great passion . <end>
<start> We must understand how a certain modicum of coldness , lucidity , and hardness is inseparable from all classical taste : above all consistency , happy intellectuality , the three unities , concentration , hatred of all feeling , of all sentimentality , of all esprit , hatred of all , of all uncertainty , evasiveness , and of all nebulosity , as also of all brevity , finishing , prettiness and good nature . <end>
<start> Artistic formulas must not be played with : life must be remodelled so that it should be forced to formulate itself accordingly . <end>
<start> It is really an exhilarating spectacle which we have only learned to laugh at quite recently , because we have only seen through it quite recently : this spectacle of Herder s , Winckelmann s , Goethe s , and Hegel s contemporaries claiming that they had rediscovered the classical ideal . <end>
<start> and at the same time , Shakespeare ! <end>
<start> And this same crew of men had scurvy repudiated all relationship with the classical school of France ! <end>
<start> As if the essential principle could not have been learnt as well here as elsewhere ! <end>
<start> But what people wanted was nature , and naturalness : Oh , the stupidity of it ! <end>
<start> It was thought that classicism was a kind of naturalness ! <end>
<start> Without either prejudice or indulgence we should try and investigate upon what soil a classical taste can be evolved . <end>
<start> The hardening , the simplification , the strengthening , and the of man are inseparable from classical taste . <end>
